## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv/dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping/self-excitation), and possibly time t (external driving), combining linear and nonlinear mechanical force terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force with linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillator with nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-cubic dissipation)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametric excitation)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Driven damped nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5) (general forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force with damping)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (general polynomial restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power terms in position (x²) → asymmetric potential indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Velocity-position coupling (x²·v) → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillations
- Trigonometric time dependence cos(c·t) → external periodic driving force
- Sign of cubic coefficient relative to linear: same sign → hardening spring; opposite sign → softening spring with potential escape
- Products (1 - x²)·v → limit cycle behavior where damping switches sign based on amplitude
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence → non-autonomous (driven) system
- Odd functions of v in damping → energy dissipation preserving time-reversal structure at equilibrium

GT Equivalence Verification (PO27)

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0586*v³ - 0.7167*v - 0.3583*v*exp(-|v|) + 0.6686*sin(t)`

Key features of the GT:
1. A `sin(t)` term
2. A linear `v` term
3. A `v³` term
4. A `v*exp(-|v|)` term (involves absolute value)
5. No dependence on `x`

Let me check candidates systematically.

**Candidates 1-25, most involving `v*x²`, `v*x`, etc.:** For these to match GT (which has no x-dependence), all x-dependent coefficients must be zero. After zeroing x-terms:

- **Candidate 3:** Zeroing c0, c5 → `c1*v + c2*sin(c3*t+c4) + c6*v³ + c7*cos(c8*t+c9)`. This gives `c6*v³ + c1*v + sin(t)_term`. The sin and cos terms can combine to form a single sinusoid of t. Setting c3=c8=1 and choosing phases, we get `A*sin(t+φ) + c1*v + c6*v³`. This matches the `v³`, `v`, and `sin(t)` terms. But GT also has `v*exp(-|v|)` which cannot be produced. So **no match**.

**Candidates 5, 6, 7, 8, 10, 17, 18:** These are linear in v (no v³ or exp terms). Cannot match GT. **No match.**

**Candidate 9:** `c0*tanh(c1*x+c2) + c3*sin(c4*t+c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*v)+1) + c9*v³`

Set c0=0 (kill tanh term): `c3*sin(c4*t+c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*v)+1) + c9*v³`

The `log(c7*exp(c8*v)+1)` term: For the softplus function, `log(a*exp(bv)+1)`. This doesn't naturally produce `v*exp(-|v|)`. The softplus is smooth and roughly linear for large arguments. It cannot replicate the combination `-0.7167*v - 0.3583*v*exp(-|v|)` which has a kink at v=0 due to |v|. **No match.**

**Candidates 26, 40:** Include `cos(c6*sin(c7*t+c8))` - this is a complicated function of t only. With `v³` term (candidate 26) plus `v` term plus trig terms. But no `v*exp(-|v|)`. **No match.**

**Candidates 34, 29-33:** `tanh + sin + log(exp(v)+1)` variants. Same issue as candidate 9 - `log(c*exp(v)+1)` cannot produce `v*exp(-|v|)`. **No match.**

**Candidates 35-50:** Various combinations with x-dependence, `exp(sin(t))`, `log(exp(x²)+1)`, etc. None contain `v*exp(-|v|)` or anything that could produce it.

Let me reconsider whether `log(c7*exp(c8*v) + 1)` could approximate `v*exp(-|v|)` exactly. The softplus function is `log(1+e^x) ≈ x` for large x and `≈ e^x` for very negative x. Its derivative is the sigmoid. There's no parameter choice that makes `c6*log(c7*exp(c8*v)+1)` equal to `-0.7167*v - 0.3583*v*exp(-|v|)` for all v. The exp(-|v|) creates a non-analytic kink that log-exp cannot replicate.

None of the candidates contain `exp(-|v|)` or `exp(-v²)` or any term that could produce the `v*exp(-|v|)` behavior present in the GT. The GT's `v*exp(-|v|)` term is essential and non-trivial, and no candidate has the structural capacity to reproduce it.

After thorough analysis, no candidate can exactly match the GT.

[NO MATCH]

2. `v` (linear in v)
3. `v*exp(-|v|)` (v times exponential of absolute value)

- GT has `v³` and `v` terms
- GT has `sin(t)`

Let me analyze each candidate:

**Candidates with x-dependence (1-4, 11-25, 26, 35-49):** These contain terms like `v*x²`, `v*x`, `x`, `x³`, etc. For these to match GT, all x-dependent coefficients must be set to 0. But then the remaining terms must reproduce the GT, which includes `v³` and `v*exp(-|v|)`.
